Marriage as a Cause for Inheritance and Blood Revenge
Ruling with reasoning (ta'lil) on spouses' rights in qisas and diya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that a valid cause (sabab) for inheritance also establishes the right to retaliation and blood money, and explain the analogy to lineage.

Core Idea
Marriage establishes a legal cause for inheritance, which in turn gives the spouse the right to qisas and diya.

In this passage, the author explains why marriage, though not a blood relationship, is treated like lineage for the purposes of retaliation and blood money. The key is that marriage is a valid cause (sabab) for inheritance, and that inheritance right extends to blood revenge. This demonstrates how a sabab in Hanafi usul can generate multiple legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
State that qisas and diya are obligatory for spouses due to marriage.
This is the ruling being justified.
2
Identify the dalil
Marriage is a cause (sabab) for khilafa (inheritance) and dark al-tha’r (blood revenge).
The text says 'because marriage is a valid cause for inheritance and blood revenge.'
3
Analyze the reasoning
Marriage has a special quality affecting ownership (tasarruf fi al-milk), making it like lineage (nasab).
This is the analogy (qiyas) grounding the extension from inheritance to blood money.
4
Note the ta'lil
The analogy shows that the legal effect (hukm) of marriage in these matters is similar to lineage.
The 'illa is the effect on ownership.
5
Conclude the principle
Any cause that establishes inheritance may also establish rights of retaliation and diya.
This is a broader usul principle derivable from the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا وجب القصاص للزوج والزوجة؛ لأن النكاح يصلح سبباً للخلافة، ودَرْك الثأر. ولهذا وجب بالزوجية نصيب في الدية، ألا يُرى أن للزوجية مزية تصرف في الملك، فصار كالنسب. وأما أحكام الآخرة فأربعة أيضاً: ١ - ما يجب له. ٢- وما يجب عليه مما اكتسبه في حياته. ٣- وما يلقاه من ثواب وكرامة. ٤- أو عقاب ومَلامة؛ لأن القبر للميت كالرَّحم للماء، والمهاد للطفل، وضع فيه لأحكام الآخرة ؛ روضة دار، أو حفرة نار، فكان له حكم الأحياء، وذلك كله بعد ما يمضي عليه في هذا المنزل الابتلاء في الابتداء ؛ تنزيهاً لشأنه، ومباهاةً له على أخدانه وأقرانه، ونرجو الله تعالى أن يصيره لنا روضةً بكرمه وفضله، والله أعلم.
For this reason qisas is obligatory for the husband and wife because marriage is a valid cause for inheritance and blood revenge. And for this reason through marriage a share in blood money becomes obligatory; do you not see that marriage has a special quality that affects ownership, so it becomes like lineage. And as for rulings of the Hereafter, they are also four: 1. What is due to him. 2. And what is due upon him from what he earned in his life. 3. And what he meets of reward and honor. 4. Or punishment and blame. Because the grave for the dead is like the womb for water, and the cradle for the child; it is placed for rulings of the Hereafter: a garden of paradise or a pit of fire. So he has the ruling of the living. And all that after he passes through this station of trial in the beginning; to exalt his status and to boast him over his peers and companions. And we hope that Allah will make it a garden for us by His generosity and favor. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 741

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with reasoning (ta'lil). The author first explains why marriage gives spouses the right to qisas (retaliation) in cases of homicide: because marriage makes the spouse eligible for inheritance (khilafa) and blood revenge (dari al-tha'r), meaning the spouse is considered a relative entitled to claim retaliation. Then it extends this to a share in blood money (diya), arguing that marriage has a special quality that affects ownership, similar to lineage (nasab). The text then shifts to discuss the rulings of the afterlife (Ahkam al-Akhira), listing four aspects: what is owed to the deceased (e.g., rights of others), what the deceased owes from his lifetime (e.g., debts), the reward or punishment he receives, and the state of the grave as either a garden or pit of fire. The grave is compared to a womb for water and a cradle for a child, emphasizing that the deceased has rulings similar to the living. This discussion is part of the broader usul topic of legal capacity (ahliyya) and the impediments that affect it, though here the focus is on the posthumous state.

Key Terms
الخِلافة (al-khilāfa): Inheritance or succession, particularly the right to inherit from the deceased.
دَرْك الثأر (dārk al-tha’r): Blood revenge or retaliation; the right to demand qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the text say qisas is obligatory for the husband and wife due to marriage?
A) Because marriage creates a right to inheritance and blood revenge
B) Because marriage is a contract that requires retaliation
C) Because spouses are considered blood relatives
D) Because marriage nullifies qisas

Key Takeaway
Marriage, as a sabab for inheritance, creates the right to qisas and diya.

The Four Afterlife Rulings (Ahkam al-Akhira)
Definition and categorization of afterlife rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories of afterlife rulings and explain why the deceased has a legal capacity (ahliyya) in the grave.

Core Idea
The grave is a station of trial where the deceased has rulings similar to the living, including rights and duties.

This passage addresses the legal capacity (ahliyya) of the deceased in the afterlife. The author lists four categories of rulings that apply after death: what is due to the deceased, what is due from him, reward, and punishment. The grave is likened to a womb or cradle, indicating a transitional state.

Guided Path
1
List the four categories
Memorize: (1) What is due to the deceased (ma lahu), (2) What is due from him (ma 'alayhi), (3) Reward and honor, (4) Punishment and blame.
These are the four Ahkam al-Akhira.
2
Understand the reason
The grave is like a womb for water or a cradle for a child, implying a developmental state where the deceased is 'alive' in some sense.
This justifies applying rulings to the deceased.
3
Note the purpose
To exalt the deceased and demonstrate his status before creation.
The text says 'to exalt his status and to boast him over his peers.'
4
Reflect on the usul principle
The deceased retains a limited legal capacity for these four matters.
This is part of the topic of ahliyya in usul.

10 min
The Requirement of Knowledge in Khiyar al-Shart: Notification Rulings
Explains khiyar al-shart and conditions for valid cancellation notification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that rescission under khiyar al-shart requires the other party's knowledge, and distinguish the conditions for valid notification by a messenger versus a mediator (fuduli).

Core Idea
Rescission imposes an obligation; thus the other party's knowledge is essential for valid cancellation under khiyar al-shart.

This passage from Usul al-Bazdawi first establishes a principle by comparing two types of options: the emancipated woman's ignorance is excused because the evidence is hidden, but the minor virgin's ignorance is not. This principle sets the stage for khiyar al-shart: rescission is an act that imposes an obligation, so it cannot be done secretly. The school then discusses how the other party must be notified—whether by a messenger (unconditionally valid within three days) or by a mediator (fuduli) for whom Abu Hanifa requires reliability or a specific number.

Guided Path
1
Identify the underlying principle
The passage contrasts two cases: emancipated woman (ignorance excused because evidence hidden) vs minor virgin (ignorance not excused because evidence well-known). This establishes that the legal effect of an option depends on the notoriety of its evidence.
This principle is the 'asl' for the later ruling on khiyar al-shart.
2
Apply the principle to khiyar al-shart
The author states that rescission without the other party's presence is invalid because it imposes an obligation (ilzam). Thus, the principle is extended: rescission requires the other party's knowledge.
The option only makes the contract non-binding; rescission is a separate act that undoes it.
3
Distinguish methods of notification
Two methods are discussed: a messenger (rasul) is valid unconditionally within three days; a mediator (fuduli) is valid only under certain conditions according to Abu Hanifa.
A messenger is authorized by the option-holder; a fuduli acts on his own.
4
Analyze the internal dispute on the fuduli
Abu Hanifa conditions either 'adalah (reliability) or a specific number (e.g., two witnesses) for the fuduli. Muhammad al-Shaybani does not require any condition. Abu Yusuf holds a different view: the option-holder is authorized to rescind unilaterally.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (thamarah al-khilaf affects validity of rescission).
5
Determine the practical consequence
If a fuduli is unreliable or unknown, Abu Hanifa says rescission is invalid; Muhammad says it is valid. This directly impacts whether the contract is effectively rescinded.
The text does not give a tarjih; both positions are recorded in zahir al-riwayah.

وأبو يوسف رحمه الله جَعَلَ صاحب خيار الشرط مسلّطاً على الفسخ من قبل صاحبه، فأضيف ما يُلزم صاحبَه إلى التزامه.
Knowledge (of the option) upon emancipation is made an excuse because the evidence is hidden regarding her, and because she is defending. Contrary to the minor virgin if she reaches puberty and her brother has married her off, and she does not know of the option, she is not excused, and her silence is considered consent, because the evidence of knowledge regarding her is well-known, not concealed, and because she thereby intends to initiate rescission, not to defend herself, and the emancipated woman repels the increase from herself. Therefore, the two options differ in the condition of judicial proceedings. And upon this principle, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) said regarding the person with the option of stipulation in a sale if he rescinds the contract without the presence of his partner: That is not valid except in his presence, because the option was established to exclude the ruling of the contract due to lack of choice, so the contract becomes non-binding thereby, then it is rescinded due to the loss of bindingness, not that the option is definitely for rescission. Hence, by rescission he is acting upon the other in a way that entails obligation, so it is not valid without his knowledge. If the messenger of the person with the option reaches him, it is valid within three days without any condition of reliability. And after three days, it is not valid. And if a mediator (fuduli) reaches him, Abu Hanifa conditions number or reliability, contrary to Muhammad. If either is found, the notification is valid within three days, and the rescission is executed; after three days, it is not valid and the rescission is void. And Abu Yusuf made the person with the option of stipulation authorized to rescind from his side, so what obligates his partner is attributed to his commitment.
Source pages p. 755

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Bazdawi discusses rulings related to khiyar (option) in contracts, particularly the option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart). The author begins by comparing two types of options: the option upon emancipation (khiyar al-'itq) and the option of a minor virgin when she reaches puberty. For an emancipated woman, ignorance of her option is excused because the evidence for it (the hadith of Barirah) is not widely known; she is in a defensive position. In contrast, a minor virgin who reaches puberty and was married by her brother is not excused for ignorance because the evidence is well-known, and she is seeking to initiate rescission, not defend herself. This difference affects whether a judicial decree is required.

Building on this principle, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani rule that if a person with khiyar al-shart in a sale rescinds the contract without the other party being present, it is invalid because the option is intended to make the contract non-binding, but rescission imposes an obligation (i.e., undoing the contract) on the other party, which requires their knowledge. Therefore, rescission must occur in the presence of the other party or with proper notification.

Notification can be done by a messenger, and within the three-day option period, it is valid without any condition on the messenger's reliability. After three days, notification by messenger is invalid. If the notification is done by a mediator (fuduli) — a third party who acts on his own initiative — Abu Hanifa requires either that the mediator is known to be reliable (adalah) or that there is a specific number of mediators (e.g., two witnesses), whereas Muhammad does not require such conditions. If the mediator meets Abu Hanifa's conditions, the notification is valid within three days; after three days, it is invalid. Abu Yusuf holds a different view: the person with the option is authorized to rescind from his side, meaning his rescission is effective and the obligation on the other party is attributed to his own commitment (i.e., he is bound by it). This passage highlights the Hanafi internal differences on khiyar al-shart and emphasizes the importance of knowledge and consent in contract rescission.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): The option of stipulation in a contract, where a party has the right to rescind within a specified period (usually three days).
فضولي (fuduli): A mediator or third party who acts without prior authorization from the principal.
عدالة (adalah): Reliability or uprightness of character; a condition for certain legal capacities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what condition must be met for a mediator (fuduli) to validly notify the other party of cancellation under khiyar al-shart within the three-day period?
A) The mediator must be a relative of the option-holder.
B) The mediator must have 'adalah (reliability) or there must be a specific number (e.g., two witnesses).
C) The mediator must be the seller.
D) The mediator must be appointed by a judge.

Key Takeaway
Rescission under khiyar al-shart requires the other party's knowledge; a fuduli must be reliable or multiple to ensure proper notification.
